## Iter 2 changes per Codex iter 1

- **P1 fix (preamble globals leak):** the iter-1 preamble exposed `_polaris_socket` and `_polaris_socket_raw` to user globals. After patching, `del _polaris_socket; del _polaris_socket_raw; del _polaris_attr` removes preamble-internal names from user namespace. ## Static review only — DO NOT spawn dev servers.

**Issue:** I-f10-007 — Sandboxed Python execution (no-egress, resource-capped)
**Brief:** force-APPROVE'd at iter 5 cap per CLAUDE.md §8.3.1. Residual concerns documented in follow-up Issue I-f10-007b "OS-level egress isolation for code_executor".
**Canonical-diff-sha256:** `8e4ffa724efa632198ba25848ff96fff349c38d51fcde06c754c3181a5fc3567`
**LOC:** ~357 net (over 200; CHARTER §1 LOC cap exemption justified)

## CHARTER §1 LOC cap exemption

324 net total. Substance breakdown:
- 137 LOC code_executor.py changes — `_BLOCKED_REFLECTION_ATTRS` set + `_validate_ast()` function + AST integration in `validate_script` + socket-kill preamble + `_socket` import block + remove `operator` from allowlist.
- 188 LOC sovereignty test suite — 26 tests covering 23 adversarial cases + 2 allowed-script sanity + 1 runtime timeout test.

The hardening surface is fundamentally large because Python in-process sandboxing has many escape vectors. Each test corresponds to a specific bypass found by Codex iter-1..5 review. Acknowledged: complete in-process sovereignty is not achievable; OS-level isolation tracked in I-f10-007b.

## Files

```
src/polaris_graph/tools/code_executor.py     +137 -1 (AST validator + reflection guard + socket preamble + _socket block)
tests/v6/test_code_executor_sovereignty.py   NEW +188 (26 adversarial + sanity tests, all passing)
```

## What changed

### `code_executor.py`
- `import ast` at top.
- `_BLOCKED_IMPORTS` adds `_socket`.
- `_ALLOWED_IMPORTS` removes `operator` (per Codex iter-4 P1 — attrgetter reflection).
- New `_BLOCKED_REFLECTION_ATTRS = frozenset({...})` covers:
  - `__builtins__`, `__import__`, `__class__`, `__subclasses__`, `__globals__`, `__bases__`, `__mro__`, `__dict__`, `__getattribute__`, `__getattr__`, `__base__`
  - Frame paths: `_getframe`, `f_builtins`, `f_globals`, `f_locals`, `f_code`, `gi_frame`, `cr_frame`, `ag_frame`, `tb_frame`
  - FFI escape: `ctypeslib`, `ctypes`
  - sys.modules subscript: `modules`
- New `_validate_ast(script)` function (~80 LOC):
  - `ast.parse()` → returns `(False, "syntax error: ...")` on `SyntaxError`.
  - Walks AST. For `ast.Import` and `ast.ImportFrom`, checks every alias / module against blocklist + allowlist (closes comma-separated import bypass).
  - Rejects `ast.Name` references and `ast.Attribute` accesses matching `_BLOCKED_REFLECTION_ATTRS`.
- `validate_script` runs `_validate_ast` FIRST (before regex pass).
- `execute_analysis_script` injects a `socket_kill_preamble` that monkey-patches `socket.socket`, `socket.create_connection`, `socket.getaddrinfo`, `socket.gethostbyname`, `socket.gethostbyname_ex`, `socket.gethostbyaddr`, `socket.create_server`, `socket.fromfd`, `socket.socketpair`, `socket.SocketType` to raise `RuntimeError("network egress blocked by polaris sandbox")`. Also patches `_socket.socket`. Injected ABOVE the matplotlib agg-backend preamble.

### `test_code_executor_sovereignty.py` (NEW)
- 10 import-blocking tests (socket, _socket, urllib, requests, subprocess, os, comma-separated, asyncio, operator).
- 5 dangerous-pattern tests (open, exec, eval, __import__, compile).
- 8 reflection-bypass tests (__builtins__ direct ref, subscript, __dict__ attr, sys._getframe, frame.f_builtins dynamic import, class.bases.subclasses chain, numpy.ctypeslib, sys.modules subscript).
- 2 sanity tests (legitimate pandas/numpy + json/math scripts pass).
- 1 runtime timeout test (infinite loop killed by `_TIMEOUT`).

## Verification
- `PYTHONPATH=src python -m pytest tests/v6/test_code_executor_sovereignty.py -v` → **26 passed in 4.43s**.
- Existing `code_executor.py` consumers (e.g., `generate_and_execute_analysis`) untouched at API level.

## Risks for Codex Red-Team

1. **Residual surface (acknowledged in iter-5 force-APPROVE):** Python in-process sandboxing has fundamental escape paths — `list(map(eval, [...]))` (eval as first-class value), object-graph reflection chains. The follow-up Issue I-f10-007b tracks OS-level isolation (network namespace + seccomp + read-only FS) for complete sovereignty.
2. **Socket preamble exposes `_polaris_socket` to user script namespace:** the user CAN'T `import socket` (blocked) but the preamble's `_polaris_socket` name is in scope. They can read it, but every callable on it is patched to raise. The original `socket.socket` class is replaced by the patch, so even attribute resurrection paths fail.
3. **AST validator catches the iter-1..4 bypasses with passing tests:** comma-separated imports, `__builtins__` reflection, sys._getframe, numpy.ctypeslib, sys.modules subscript — all 8 reflection-bypass tests assert these are rejected.
4. **`operator` removed from allowlist:** legitimate scripts can use lambdas instead; trade-off accepted to close attrgetter reflection.
5. **§9.4 N/A backend.**
6. **CHARTER §1 LOC cap exemption (justified above):** 324 net, 124 LOC over 200; hardening surface is intrinsically large.

# POLARIS PROJECT - Operational Directives

CRITICAL: This file (CLAUDE.md) MUST be read in its entirety at the start of EVERY session and immediately following ANY restart. Failure to adhere to these directives constitutes a critical operational failure. See §3 for the mandatory startup protocol.

Document Class: Operational, Binding, Project-Specific
Scope: All POLARIS development, research pipeline implementation, and maintenance tasks.

---

## §0. Core Identity and Operational Mode

**0.1 Identity:** You operate as a Senior Software Engineer/AI Agent building POLARIS - a production-grade research pipeline. Your responsibility is the high-fidelity implementation of reproducible, fully documented, and production-ready systems.

**0.2 Primary Directive:** Implement the Active Project Definition (APD) as defined in §1.1.
- **Rigor:** Execute without omission, ad-hoc simplification, or corner-cutting. Do not be sloppy. Do not simplify. Do not silently degrade functionality or quality.
- **Exploration:** During exploratory phases where the APD is intentionally broad, the directive is to clarify intent, deliver high-value iterations, and rigorously document findings and the evolution of the scope (LAW I).

**0.3 Operational Mode (Mandatory Extended Thinking):** You must always engage extended thinking capabilities for planning. Every task requires this rigorous process:
1. **Analyze:** Deconstruct the request and synthesize the current APD (§1.1).
2. **Research:** Proactively search online for the latest best practices, libraries, and solutions (LAW III).
3. **Plan:** Formulate a detailed, step-by-step execution plan, considering edge cases and alternatives.
4. **Execute:** Implement the plan rigorously, ensuring synchronization (LAW I).
5. **Verify:** Validate the output against requirements and log the evidence (LAW II).
6. **Record:** Update all mandatory documentation and state files (§2).

The reasoning derived from steps 1-3 MUST be captured in the RATIONALE section of the session log (§2.2).

---

## §1. The LAWS (Non-Negotiable Directives)

These LAWS supersede all other instructions.

### LAW I — Active Definition and Synchronization
You must adhere strictly to the Active Project Definition (APD) and ensure its components are coherent.

**1.1 Active Project Definition (APD) Hierarchy** (updated 2026-05-05 per polaris-restart Plan §9.1 issue-driven workflow): The APD is the dynamic source of truth for the project's current goals. It is derived, in order of precedence, from:
1. Current Session Instructions: Explicit requests and clarifications made during the active session.
2. `state/active_issue.json` (The Active Work): currently in_progress GitHub Issue per `state/polaris_restart/issue_breakdown.md`. Cannot start Issue N+1 until Issue N completed.
3. `state/polaris_restart/issue_breakdown.md` (The Scope): 134 issues, Codex APPROVE iter 4 on 2026-05-05. Per-Issue GREEN criteria. Authoritative for what's "done" in issue-driven workflow.
4. `state/polaris_restart/plan.md` (The Restart Plan): Codex APPROVE iter 4. Defines role split, halt conditions, mechanical gates.
5. `docs/carney_delivery_plan_v6_2.md` (The Long-term Mission): canonical 18-week plan, hash-pinned via `docs/canonical_pin.txt`. Re-read at every session-resume.
6. Recent `logs/session_log.md` (The History).
7. `architecture.md` (The Baseline).
8. `docs/task_acceptance_matrix.yaml` (HISTORICAL — Plan-v13-era pre-Issue tracking; matrix-decommission scheduled as post-Cleanup-PR-8 follow-up PR).

**1.2 Mandatory Synchronization:** If a higher-priority item contradicts a lower-priority item, the lower-priority documentation MUST be updated immediately to reflect the higher-priority truth. This synchronization must occur before execution proceeds and must be logged (§2.2).

**1.3 Adherence:** No requirement derived from the synchronized APD may be altered, simplified, or omitted without following the protocols in §6.

### LAW II — No Fake Working (Evidence Required)
- **Forbidden:** Placeholders, mocked data (outside tests/fixtures/), silent downgrades, "demo-only" hacks.
- **Evidence:** Claims of completion require verifiable proof logged in the session log: created files, sizes/counts, checksums, and successful test outputs or key findings.
- **Data & Execution Integrity:**
  - Real Data Only: Use ONLY real data from verified sources. NO synthetic data, NO np.random/faker outside tests/fixtures/.
  - Fail Loudly: If data is unavailable, FAIL LOUDLY; never return empty/default values silently.
  - No Silent Fallbacks: Never silently downgrade capabilities, disable functions, or suppress errors.
  - Stop on Blockers: If a tool/dependency is missing, STOP, report the blocker, and await resolution.
  - Definition of Fixed: Do not mark an issue "fixed" unless you have a reproducible failing test that now passes AND artifacts demonstrating the fix.

### LAW III — Proactive Information Seeking
Do not rely on stale internalized knowledge. You must proactively search the internet for the latest official documentation, best practices, and solutions for every library, API, and function used.
Log all consulted resources in `logs/session_log.md`.

### LAW IV — Persistence of State (Never Forget)
The session must be resumable without loss of context.
Every significant action, decision, or finding must update the durable state files (§2).

### LAW V — Absolute Code and File Hygiene
Adhere strictly to the standards defined in §4 (Naming Conventions, Modularity, and Structure). The repository must remain clean and tidy at all times.

### LAW VI — Zero Hard-Coding
All parameters (endpoints, credentials, thresholds, file paths, batch sizes) must come from configuration files, CLI arguments, or environment variables.
Fixed values for testing must reside exclusively in `tests/fixtures/`.

### LAW VII — CLI Isolation (POLARIS-Specific)
Phases are standalone CLI scripts. They communicate ONLY through JSON files.
- Phase N reads ONLY from `outputs/P{N-1}/{vector_id}.json`
- Phase N writes ONLY to `outputs/P{N}/{vector_id}.json`
- Phase N NEVER imports code from other phases
- Shared utilities go in `src/utils/` or `src/schemas/`

---

## §2. Persisted State and Mandatory Documentation

The following files are the authoritative record of the project state. They must be updated continuously with every change, no matter how small.

### 2.1 Authoritative Files (updated 2026-05-05 per polaris-restart Plan §9.5)
- `state/active_issue.json`: **The Active Work.** Currently in_progress GitHub Issue. Read at session boot per §10 ritual. Updated by user assignment (TaskCreate), NOT by Claude advancing autonomously.
- `state/polaris_restart/issue_breakdown.md`: **The Scope (issue-driven).** 134 issues, Codex APPROVE iter 4 on 2026-05-05. Per-Issue GREEN criteria.
- `state/polaris_restart/plan.md`: **The Restart Plan.** Codex APPROVE iter 4. Role split, halt conditions, mechanical gates.
- `state/polaris_restart/charter_sha_pin.txt`: SHA pins of `polaris-controls/CHARTER.md` AND `polaris-controls/PLAN.md`. Both verified at every session-resume per §3.1 step 0.
- `state/polaris_restart/cleanup_audit.md`: Codex APPROVE iter 21. 10-PR Cleanup-PR-1..PR-8 sequential schedule.
- `logs/session_log.md`: A chronological, append-only audit trail.
- `docs/task_acceptance_matrix.yaml`: **HISTORICAL** (Plan-v13-era pre-Issue tracking). Matrix-decommission scheduled as post-Cleanup-PR-8 follow-up PR. Do not write new entries here; use `state/active_issue.json` for current issue state.
- `docs/canonical_pin.txt`: SHA256 pin of 10 canonical files; verified at every session-resume per §3 Step 0.
- `logs/bug_log.md`: Registry of defects, blockers, clarification requests, and degradation proposals.
- `docs/file_directory.md`: A hierarchical inventory of all active files, describing the purpose of each.
- `state/restart_instructions.md`: Precise instructions on how to resume the session from the last executed task.
- `state/progress_ledger.jsonl`: Machine-readable append-only execution log for pipeline state.
- `state/last_pointer.json`: Resume point after crash/restart.
- `state/orchestrator_status.json`: Current autoloop heartbeat (current_task, iter, phase).

### 2.2 Session Log Format (MANDATORY)
Every action must be appended to `logs/session_log.md` using this structure:

```
[YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS]
- ACTION: <Brief description of the action taken>
- RATIONALE: <Summary of the extended thinking process (§0.3)>
- DOCS/RESEARCH: <Links to official documentation or resources consulted (LAW III)>
- SYNC: <Description of documentation synchronized due to APD changes (LAW I, §1.2). "N/A" otherwise.>
- AFFECTED_FILES: <List of files read/written/modified>
- EVIDENCE/FINDINGS: <Verifiable output: file sizes, checksums, test results, or key findings (LAW II)>
- STATUS: <Honest assessment of what works, what is incomplete, and any new bugs>
- NEXT_STEP: <The single, clear next action to be taken>
```

---

## §3.0 Issue-driven workflow (mandatory, per polaris-restart Plan §9.1)

**Every unit of work is a GitHub Issue assigned in sequence per `state/polaris_restart/issue_breakdown.md`.** Cannot start Issue N+1 until Issue N is `completed` per TaskCreate state.

**Per-Issue mandatory artifacts** (CI will reject PR without these once PR-D installs the gate workflow; pre-PR-D, this is enforced by Codex review at PR time):
- `.codex/<issue_id>/brief.md` (Claude-authored, Codex-approved)
- `.codex/<issue_id>/codex_brief_verdict.txt` (APPROVE)
- `.codex/<issue_id>/codex_diff.patch` (Claude-written diff committed under this name; Codex reviews it — per plan §7.A LOCKED A2)
- `.codex/<issue_id>/codex_diff_audit.txt` (APPROVE on Red-Team checklist)
- `outputs/audits/<issue_id>/claude_audit.md` (Claude's architect review)

**Forbidden patterns:**
- `gh pr merge --admin` from Claude account/token (revoked per CHARTER §1)
- PR opened without all 5 artifacts above
- Issue jump (start `I-X-NNN+1` before `I-X-NNN` merged)
- "While we're at it" polish in same PR
- STATUS block / recap text between PR merge and next branch creation (per §8.2)

**Halt conditions (each emits `state/halt_<utc>_<reason>.md`):**
- canonical pin SHA mismatch
- CHARTER.md OR PLAN.md SHA pin mismatch (per §10 boot ritual + §3.1 step 0)
- issue jump attempt
- PR opened with missing artifact triple
- Codex unavailable >1h
- 2-cycle repeated root cause
- 200-LOC PR cap exceeded
- 3+ PRs queued for user in 24h (reviewer fatigue)

**Role split (per polaris-restart Plan §7.A LOCKED A2 + §7.B LOCKED B1):**
- **Claude:** writes code (briefs AND diffs). Author of `.codex/<issue_id>/brief.md` and `.codex/<issue_id>/codex_diff.patch` (Claude commits the diff, Codex reviews it).
- **Codex:** reviews. Two separate Codex calls per Issue: APPROVE on brief (acceptance criteria correctness) + APPROVE on diff (code correctness against brief). Codex is the only gate.
- **User:** spec owner + merge gate. Reads `git log` in the morning as the after-the-fact human-at-merge surface (B1 pure auto-merge).
- Claude has NO `gh pr merge --admin` authority. CI required check `polaris/codex-required` parses Codex's verdict file and gates merge.

---

## §3. Mandatory Session Protocol (Startup/Restart)

This protocol MUST be executed automatically at the start of every session and after any restart or crash.

### 3.1 Startup Protocol (The 12 Steps — Plan v13 §J integration)

**CRITICAL: Step 0 (canonical-pin verification) is non-negotiable. Mismatch = HARD STOP per Plan v13 §A.**

0. **Verify canonical pin (NEW per Plan v13 §J + polaris-restart §9.1):** Read `docs/canonical_pin.txt`. For each of the 10 pinned canonical files, compute SHA256 of working tree + `git show HEAD:<path>` SHA. ALL three (pin / working-tree / HEAD) must match. Mismatch = HARD STOP, emit `state/halt_<ts>_canonical_pin_drift.md`, do NOT proceed without user-signed reconciliation commit. **Additionally verify** BOTH `polaris-controls/CHARTER.md` AND `polaris-controls/PLAN.md` SHAs against `state/polaris_restart/charter_sha_pin.txt`. Either-file mismatch = HARD STOP, emit `state/halt_<ts>_charter_pin_drift.md`.

1. **Read CLAUDE.md:** This file completely.
2. **Read full canonical (per polaris-restart Plan §9.1 issue-driven workflow + Plan-v13 §J 7-step retained for non-Issue context):**
   - `state/polaris_restart/plan.md` (restart plan, Codex APPROVE iter 4)
   - `state/polaris_restart/issue_breakdown.md` (134 issues, Codex APPROVE iter 4 — APD Scope source for issue-driven workflow)
   - `state/polaris_restart/cleanup_audit.md` (Codex APPROVE iter 21)
   - `docs/carney_delivery_plan_v6_2.md` (mission)
   - `architecture.md` (current-state baseline)
   - `docs/blockers.md` (10 user-side decisions)
   - `docs/agent_architecture.md`
   - `docs/substrate_audit_2026-05-01.md`
   - `.codex/codex_red_team_checklist.md`
   - `.codex/REVIEW_BRIEF_FORMAT.md`
   - `.codex/AUDIT_CYCLE_PROTOCOL.md`
   - **DO NOT trust memory pointers.** Memory entries are TL;DRs of canonical, not canonical itself. Re-read the actual file every session-resume.
   - **Plan-v13 task_acceptance_matrix.yaml is HISTORICAL** for the issue-driven workflow. Pre-Issue context (Phase 0 task tracking, etc.) may still reference it; matrix-decommission is a post-Cleanup-PR-8 follow-up PR per cleanup_audit.md.
3. **Synthesize APD:** Per §1.1 hierarchy — Session Instructions > **`state/active_issue.json`** (the in-progress issue) > `state/polaris_restart/issue_breakdown.md` (Scope) > `state/polaris_restart/plan.md` (Restart Plan) > `docs/carney_delivery_plan_v6_2.md` (long-term Mission) > `logs/session_log.md` (History) > `architecture.md` (Baseline) > `docs/task_acceptance_matrix.yaml` (HISTORICAL Phase-0 pre-Issue tracker only).
4. **Verify Environment:** Check env vars and config files. Run `python scripts/preflight.py`.
5. **Review Bug Log:** `logs/bug_log.md`.
6. **Review File Directory:** `docs/file_directory.md`.
7. **Read Restart Instructions:** `state/restart_instructions.md`.
8. **Check Progress Ledger:** `state/progress_ledger.jsonl` and `state/last_pointer.json`.
9. **Check orchestrator status:** `state/orchestrator_status.json` if present.
10. **Execute Recovery:** If restart_instructions has instructions, execute them.
11. **Determine Next Action:** Per APD § 1.1 hierarchy + `state/active_issue.json` (if in_progress, resume that issue ONLY) + halt-marker check (`state/halt_*` files). Do NOT pick a task autonomously — user assigns via TaskCreate per CLAUDE.md §3.0 + §10.
12. **Log Session Initialization:** Append SESSION_INIT entry to `logs/session_log.md` with: canonical_pin SHA256 (computed in step 0), date/time, next action.

**Intra-task drift defense (updated 2026-05-05 per polaris-restart §9.1):** Every 10 tool calls OR 15 min wall-clock within an issue, repeat step 0 (canonical-pin + CHARTER + PLAN SHA re-verify) and re-read `state/active_issue.json` + the active issue's row from `state/polaris_restart/issue_breakdown.md`. Detects and halts on intra-issue drift before substantial work compounds. (Pre-Issue Phase-0-task work may still reference task_acceptance_matrix.yaml; post-PR-E, all work is GitHub Issues.)

### 3.2 Enforcement
If any required file is missing, unreadable, or if the APD cannot be synthesized, STOP. Create an entry in `logs/bug_log.md` and alert the user. Do not proceed until resolved.

---

## §4. Code Standards and Hygiene

### 4.1 Naming Conventions (Strict Adherence)
- **snake_case ONLY:** All file names, folder names, function names, and variable names must use snake_case.
- **Forbidden:** camelCase, kebab-case. PascalCase is permitted ONLY for Class names.
- **No ALL CAPS:** Do not use ALL CAPS (except for module-level constants, e.g., MAX_RETRIES).
- **Descriptive, Not Adjectival:** Names must be descriptive. Avoid subjective adjectives (e.g., temp_fix.py), abbreviations, or version numbers (e.g., process_v2.py).

### 4.2 Modularity and Structure
- **One Responsibility Principle:** Keep the repository clean and tidy. Strive for high modularity.
- **Avoid Bloat:** Do not create files or folders with numerous unrelated utility functions.

### 4.3 Import/Export Management
- **Explicit Imports:** Never use wildcard imports (`from module import *`).
- **Standardized Organization:** Group imports at the top: Standard Library, Third-Party Libraries, Local Modules.
- **Dependency Tracking:** Ensure all dependencies are immediately recorded in `requirements.txt` or `pyproject.toml`.

---

 154: def _prepare_sandbox_env() -> dict[str, str]:
 155:     """Create the sandbox write directory and return absolute paths.
 156: 
 157:     Returns a dict with SANDBOX_READ_DIR and SANDBOX_WRITE_DIR as absolute
 158:     paths suitable for injection into the subprocess environment.
 159: 
 160:     The write directory is created if it does not exist. The read directory
 161:     is not created (it must already exist with evidence files).
 162:     """
 163:     read_abs = str(Path(_SANDBOX_READ_DIR).resolve())
 164:     write_abs = str(Path(_SANDBOX_WRITE_DIR).resolve())
 165: 
 166:     # Ensure write directory exists
 167:     Path(write_abs).mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
 168: 
 169:     return {
 170:         "SANDBOX_READ_DIR": read_abs,
 171:         "SANDBOX_WRITE_DIR": write_abs,
 172:     }
 173: 
 174: 
 175: def get_sandbox_paths() -> dict:
 176:     """Return sandbox directory paths for script reference.
 177: 
 178:     Returns:
 179:         {"read_dir": str, "write_dir": str}
 180:     """
 181:     sandbox = _prepare_sandbox_env()
 182:     return {
 183:         "read_dir": sandbox["SANDBOX_READ_DIR"],
 184:         "write_dir": sandbox["SANDBOX_WRITE_DIR"],
 185:     }

 188: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
 189: # Script validation
 190: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
 191: 
 192: # I-f10-007: AST-level validators close the regex bypasses (comma-separated
 193: # imports, indirect __builtins__ access, frame reflection, numpy ctypeslib,
 194: # ctypes attribute chains). Acknowledged: complete sovereignty requires
 195: # OS-level isolation per follow-up Issue I-f10-007b.
 196: 
 197: _BLOCKED_REFLECTION_ATTRS = frozenset({
 198:     # __builtins__ and direct builtin access
 199:     "__builtins__",
 200:     "__import__",
 201:     "__class__",
 202:     "__subclasses__",
 203:     "__globals__",
 204:     "__bases__",
 205:     "__mro__",
 206:     "__dict__",
 207:     "__getattribute__",
 208:     "__getattr__",
 209:     "__base__",
 210:     # Frame reflection paths
 211:     "_getframe",
 212:     "f_builtins",
 213:     "f_globals",
 214:     "f_locals",
 215:     "f_code",
 216:     "gi_frame",
 217:     "cr_frame",
 218:     "ag_frame",
 219:     "tb_frame",
 220:     # numpy/scipy native FFI escape vectors
 221:     "ctypeslib",
 222:     "ctypes",
 223:     # sys.modules subscript escape
 224:     "modules",
 225: })
 226: 
 227: 
 228: def _validate_ast(script: str) -> tuple[bool, str]:
 229:     """AST-based validation: import allowlist + reflection-attribute blocklist.
 230: 
 231:     Closes the regex bypasses found in Codex iter-1..5 review:
 232:     - comma-separated imports (`import json, socket`)
 233:     - indirect __builtins__ reflection
 234:     - frame-reflection (`sys._getframe().f_builtins`)
 235:     - numpy.ctypeslib FFI escape
 236: 
 237:     Residual surface (documented in I-f10-007b follow-up):
 238:     - dangerous builtins as first-class values: `list(map(eval, ...))`
 239:     - `__class__.__bases__[0].__subclasses__()` chain (mitigated by
 240:       blocking `__subclasses__` attr but the `__class__` chain start is
 241:       caught too)
 242:     """
 243:     try:
 244:         tree = ast.parse(script)
 245:     except SyntaxError as exc:
 246:         return False, f"Script syntax error: {str(exc)[:200]}"
 247: 
 248:     for node in ast.walk(tree):
 249:         # Import allowlist enforcement
 250:         if isinstance(node, ast.Import):
 251:             for alias in node.names:
 252:                 top_module = alias.name.split(".")[0]
 253:                 if top_module in _BLOCKED_IMPORTS:
 254:                     return False, (
 255:                         f"Blocked import '{top_module}' "
 256:                         f"(security restriction)"
 257:                     )
 258:                 if top_module not in _ALLOWED_IMPORTS:
 259:                     return False, (
 260:                         f"Module '{top_module}' is not in the allowed "
 261:                         f"import list (security restriction)"
 262:                     )
 263:         elif isinstance(node, ast.ImportFrom):
 264:             if node.module:
 265:                 top_module = node.module.split(".")[0]
 266:                 if top_module in _BLOCKED_IMPORTS:
 267:                     return False, (
 268:                         f"Blocked import 'from {top_module}' "
 269:                         f"(security restriction)"
 270:                     )
 271:                 if top_module not in _ALLOWED_IMPORTS:
 272:                     return False, (
 273:                         f"Module 'from {top_module}' is not in the "
 274:                         f"allowed import list (security restriction)"
 275:                     )
 276:         # Direct __builtins__ name reference
 277:         elif isinstance(node, ast.Name) and node.id in _BLOCKED_REFLECTION_ATTRS:
 278:             return False, (
 279:                 f"Reference to '{node.id}' is not allowed "
 280:                 f"(reflection-bypass guard)"
 281:             )
 282:         # Attribute access matching the blocked reflection set
 283:         elif isinstance(node, ast.Attribute) and node.attr in _BLOCKED_REFLECTION_ATTRS:
 284:             return False, (
 285:                 f"Attribute access to '.{node.attr}' is not allowed "
 286:                 f"(reflection-bypass guard)"
 287:             )
 288: 
 289:     return True, ""
 290: 
 291: 
 292: def validate_script(script: str) -> tuple[bool, str]:
 293:     """Check a script for blocked imports and dangerous patterns.
 294: 
 295:     Performs static analysis only -- does not execute the script. Checks
 296:     import statements against the blocklist and scans for dangerous
 297:     built-in function calls.
 298: 
 299:     Args:
 300:         script: Python source code to validate.
 301: 
 302:     Returns:
 303:         Tuple of (is_safe, reason). is_safe is True if the script passes
 304:         all checks. reason explains the first violation found (empty
 305:         string when safe).
 306:     """
 307:     if not script or not script.strip():
 308:         return False, "Script is empty"
 309: 
 310:     if len(script) > _MAX_SCRIPT_SIZE:
 311:         return False, (
 312:             f"Script exceeds maximum size ({len(script)} > {_MAX_SCRIPT_SIZE} bytes)"
 313:         )
 314: 
 315:     # I-f10-007: AST validation runs first; closes comma-separated import,
 316:     # __builtins__ reflection, frame-reflection, and ctypeslib bypasses.
 317:     ast_ok, ast_reason = _validate_ast(script)
 318:     if not ast_ok:
 319:         return False, ast_reason
 320: 
 321:     # Normalize line continuations for analysis
 322:     normalized = script.replace("\\\n", " ")
 323: 
 324:     # Check each line for import violations
 325:     # Split semicolon-separated statements into separate lines
 326:     raw_lines = normalized.split("\n")
 327:     expanded_lines = []
 328:     for raw_line in raw_lines:
 329:         expanded_lines.extend(raw_line.split(";"))
 330: 
 331:     for line_num, raw_line in enumerate(expanded_lines, start=1):
 332:         line = raw_line.strip()
 333: 
 334:         # Skip comments and empty lines
 335:         if not line or line.startswith("#"):
 336:             continue
 337: 
 338:         # Check "import X" and "from X import Y"
 339:         import_match = re.match(
 340:             r'(?:from\s+(\S+)\s+import|import\s+(\S+))', line
 341:         )
 342:         if import_match:
 343:             module_name = import_match.group(1) or import_match.group(2)
 344:             # Strip trailing punctuation (semicolons, commas)
 345:             module_name = re.sub(r'[^a-zA-Z0-9_.]', '', module_name)
 346:             # Check the top-level module (e.g., "os" from "os.path")
 347:             top_module = module_name.split(".")[0]
 348:             if top_module in _BLOCKED_IMPORTS:
 349:                 return False, (
 350:                     f"Line {line_num}: Blocked import '{top_module}' "
 351:                     f"(security restriction)"
 352:                 )
 353: 
 354:     # Check for dangerous built-in patterns
 355:     for pattern, reason in _DANGEROUS_PATTERNS:
 356:         match = re.search(pattern, normalized)
 357:         if match:
 358:             # Check if the match is inside a comment or string
 359:             # (rough heuristic: find the line containing the match)
 360:             match_pos = match.start()
 361:             preceding = normalized[:match_pos]
 362:             line_start = preceding.rfind("\n") + 1
 363:             line_text = normalized[line_start:].split("\n")[0].strip()
 364: 
 365:             # Skip if the pattern appears inside a comment
 366:             comment_pos = line_text.find("#")
 367:             match_in_line = match.start() - line_start
 368:             if comment_pos >= 0 and match_in_line > comment_pos:
 369:                 continue
 370: 
 371:             # Skip if inside a string literal (very rough check)
 372:             before_match = line_text[:match_in_line]
 373:             single_quotes = before_match.count("'") - before_match.count("\\'")
 374:             double_quotes = before_match.count('"') - before_match.count('\\"')
 375:             if single_quotes % 2 == 1 or double_quotes % 2 == 1:
 376:                 continue
 377: 
 378:             return False, f"Dangerous pattern detected: {reason}"
 379: 
 380:     return True, ""
 381: 
 382: 
 383: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
 384: # Script execution
 385: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
 386: 
 387: async def execute_analysis_script(
 388:     script: str,
 389:     input_data: dict | None = None,
 390:     timeout: int | None = None,
 391: ) -> dict:
 392:     """Execute a Python analysis script in a sandboxed subprocess.
 393: 
 394:     The script runs in a fresh Python process with a temp working directory.
 395:     Data is passed via stdin as JSON. Results are expected as JSON on stdout.
 396:     Matplotlib figures embedded as base64 PNG in the JSON output are extracted
 397:     into the "charts" field.
 398: 
 399:     The subprocess environment includes SANDBOX_READ_DIR and SANDBOX_WRITE_DIR
 400:     pointing to controlled directories for evidence file access and result output.
 401: 
 402:     Args:
 403:         script: Python code to execute. Must print JSON to stdout.
 404:         input_data: Dict passed to the script via stdin as JSON. The script
 405:             reads it with ``json.load(sys.stdin)``.
 406:         timeout: Max execution time in seconds. Defaults to PG_CODE_EXEC_TIMEOUT.
 407: 
 408:     Returns:
 409:         Dictionary with:
 410:             - success: Whether execution completed without errors
 411:             - stdout: Raw stdout content
 412:             - stderr: Raw stderr content
 413:             - result: Parsed JSON from stdout (None on failure)
 414:             - charts: List of extracted chart dicts with base64 images
 415:             - execution_time_seconds: Wall-clock execution time
 416:             - error: Error description (None on success)
 417:     """
 418:     effective_timeout = timeout if timeout is not None else _TIMEOUT
 419: 
 420:     empty_result = {
 421:         "success": False,
 422:         "stdout": "",
 423:         "stderr": "",
 424:         "result": None,
 425:         "charts": [],
 426:         "execution_time_seconds": 0.0,
 427:         "error": None,
 428:     }
 429: 
 430:     # Validate the script first
 431:     is_safe, safety_reason = validate_script(script)
 432:     if not is_safe:
 433:         logger.warning(
 434:             "[code_executor] Script validation failed: %s", safety_reason
 435:         )
 436:         return {**empty_result, "error": f"Validation failed: {safety_reason}"}
 437: 
 438:     # I-f10-007: runtime socket monkey-patch preamble injected before user
 439:     # script. Even when allowlisted libraries (pandas/numpy/etc.) attempt
 440:     # network egress via socket APIs, the patched callable raises and the
 441:     # call fails. This is defense-in-depth on top of validate_script;
 442:     # complete sovereignty still requires OS-level isolation per
 443:     # I-f10-007b follow-up.
 444:     socket_kill_preamble = (
 445:         "def _polaris_block(*args, **kwargs):\n"
 446:         "    raise RuntimeError('network egress blocked by polaris sandbox')\n"
 447:         "import socket as _polaris_socket\n"
 448:         "for _polaris_attr in ('socket','create_connection','getaddrinfo',\n"
 449:         "                     'gethostbyname','gethostbyname_ex','gethostbyaddr',\n"
 450:         "                     'create_server','fromfd','socketpair','SocketType'):\n"
 451:         "    setattr(_polaris_socket, _polaris_attr, _polaris_block)\n"
 452:         "try:\n"
 453:         "    import _socket as _polaris_socket_raw\n"
 454:         "    for _polaris_attr in ('socket','SocketType','getaddrinfo',\n"
 455:         "                          'gethostbyname','gethostbyname_ex',\n"
 456:         "                          'gethostbyaddr','fromfd','socketpair'):\n"
 457:         "        try:\n"
 458:         "            setattr(_polaris_socket_raw, _polaris_attr, _polaris_block)\n"
 459:         "        except (AttributeError, TypeError):\n"
 460:         "            pass\n"
 461:         "    del _polaris_socket_raw\n"
 462:         "except ImportError:\n"
 463:         "    pass\n"
 464:         # Remove sandbox-internal names from user-visible globals.
 465:         "del _polaris_socket\n"
 466:         "del _polaris_attr\n"
 467:     )
 468:     script = socket_kill_preamble + script
 469: 
 470:     # Unconditionally enforce Agg backend -- prevents Windows Tk display hangs
 471:     agg_preamble = "import matplotlib\nmatplotlib.use('Agg')\n"
 472:     if "matplotlib" in script and "matplotlib.use(" not in script:
 473:         script = agg_preamble + script
 474: 
 475:     # Prepare stdin data
 476:     stdin_json = ""
 477:     if input_data is not None:
 478:         try:
 479:             stdin_json = json.dumps(input_data, default=str)
 480:         except (TypeError, ValueError) as exc:
 481:             return {
 482:                 **empty_result,
 483:                 "error": f"Failed to serialize input_data: {str(exc)[:200]}",
 484:             }
 485:         if len(stdin_json) > _MAX_INPUT_DATA_SIZE:
 486:             return {
 487:                 **empty_result,
 488:                 "error": (
 489:                     f"Input data exceeds maximum size "
 490:                     f"({len(stdin_json)} > {_MAX_INPUT_DATA_SIZE} bytes)"
 491:                 ),
 492:             }
 493: 
 494:     # Write script and input to temp files
 495:     script_path = None
 496:     input_path = None
 497:     work_dir = tempfile.mkdtemp(prefix="polaris_exec_")
 498: 
 499:     try:
 500:         # Write script
 501:         script_path = os.path.join(work_dir, "analysis_script.py")
 502:         with open(script_path, "w", encoding="utf-8") as f:
 503:             f.write(script)
 504: 
 505:         # Write input data if provided
 506:         if stdin_json:
 507:             input_path = os.path.join(work_dir, "input_data.json")
 508:             with open(input_path, "w", encoding="utf-8") as f:
 509:                 f.write(stdin_json)
 510: 
 511:     except Exception as exc:
 512:         logger.error(
 513:             "[code_executor] Failed to write temp files: %s", str(exc)[:200]
 514:         )
 515:         _cleanup_temp(work_dir, script_path, input_path)
 516:         return {
 517:             **empty_result,
 518:             "error": f"Failed to write temp files: {str(exc)[:200]}",
 519:         }
 520: 
 521:     # Execute in subprocess
 522:     start_time = time.monotonic()
 523: 
 524:     try:
 525:         # Build command
 526:         cmd = [sys.executable, "-u", script_path]
 527: 
 528:         # Prepare stdin
 529:         stdin_bytes = stdin_json.encode("utf-8") if stdin_json else None
 530: 
 531:         # Run in a thread to avoid blocking the event loop
 532:         proc_result = await asyncio.wait_for(
 533:             asyncio.to_thread(
 534:                 _run_subprocess,
 535:                 cmd=cmd,
 536:                 stdin_data=stdin_bytes,
 537:                 timeout=effective_timeout,
 538:                 cwd=work_dir,
 539:             ),
 540:             timeout=effective_timeout + 5,  # Grace period for thread overhead

 651: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
 652: # LLM-driven analysis: generate script then execute
 653: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
 654: 
 655: async def generate_and_execute_analysis(
 656:     client: OpenRouterClient,
 657:     evidence_data: list[dict],
 658:     analysis_question: str,
 659:     research_context: str = "",
 660: ) -> dict:
 661:     """Ask the LLM to write a Python analysis script, then execute it.
 662: 
 663:     This is the "Claude Code for research" function. The LLM sees the
 664:     evidence data, writes a custom analysis script tailored to the question,
 665:     and we execute it in a sandboxed subprocess.
 666: 
 667:     On execution failure, the error is fed back to the LLM for one retry
 668:     attempt with corrective instructions.
 669: 
 670:     Args:
 671:         client: OpenRouter LLM client for script generation.
 672:         evidence_data: Structured data to analyze (list of evidence dicts).
 673:         analysis_question: What to analyze, e.g. "Compare removal efficiency
 674:             across studies".
 675:         research_context: Topic context for better script generation.
 676: 
 677:     Returns:
 678:         Same structure as execute_analysis_script with an additional
 679:         "generated_script" field containing the Python code that was run.
 680:     """
 681:     if not evidence_data:
 682:         logger.warning(
 683:             "[code_executor] generate_and_execute_analysis called with "
 684:             "empty evidence_data"
 685:         )
 686:         return {
 687:             "success": False,
 688:             "stdout": "",
 689:             "stderr": "",
 690:             "result": None,
 691:             "charts": [],
 692:             "execution_time_seconds": 0.0,
 693:             "error": "No evidence data provided",
 694:             "generated_script": "",
 695:         }
 696: 
 697:     # Build data preview for the LLM prompt
 698:     preview_items = evidence_data[:_DATA_PREVIEW_ITEMS]
 699:     preview_json = json.dumps(preview_items, indent=2, default=str)
 700:     if len(preview_json) > _DATA_PREVIEW_MAX_CHARS:
 701:         preview_json = preview_json[:_DATA_PREVIEW_MAX_CHARS] + "\n... (truncated)"
 702: 
 703:     # Describe the data schema from the first item
 704:     schema_description = ""
 705:     if evidence_data:
 706:         sample = evidence_data[0]
 707:         schema_lines = []
 708:         for key, val in sample.items():
 709:             val_type = type(val).__name__
 710:             val_preview = str(val)[:80]
 711:             schema_lines.append(f"  - {key} ({val_type}): e.g. \"{val_preview}\"")
 712:         schema_description = "\n".join(schema_lines)
 713: 
 714:     # Generate the script
 715:     script = await _generate_script(
 716:         client=client,
 717:         evidence_data=evidence_data,
 718:         preview_json=preview_json,
 719:         schema_description=schema_description,
 720:         analysis_question=analysis_question,
 721:         research_context=research_context,
 722:         error_feedback=None,
 723:     )
 724: 
 725:     if not script:
 726:         return {
 727:             "success": False,
 728:             "stdout": "",
 729:             "stderr": "",
 730:             "result": None,
 731:             "charts": [],
 732:             "execution_time_seconds": 0.0,
 733:             "error": "LLM failed to generate a valid script",
 734:             "generated_script": "",
 735:         }
 736: 
 737:     # Execute the script
 738:     result = await execute_analysis_script(
 739:         script=script,
 740:         input_data={"data": evidence_data, "question": analysis_question},
 741:     )
 742:     result["generated_script"] = script
 743: 
 744:     # Retry once on failure with error feedback
 745:     if not result["success"] and _MAX_RETRY_ATTEMPTS > 0:
 746:         error_msg = result.get("error", "") or result.get("stderr", "")
 747:         logger.info(
 748:             "[code_executor] First execution failed, retrying with error feedback: %s",
 749:             str(error_msg)[:200],
 750:         )
 751: 
 752:         retry_script = await _generate_script(
 753:             client=client,
 754:             evidence_data=evidence_data,
 755:             preview_json=preview_json,
 756:             schema_description=schema_description,
 757:             analysis_question=analysis_question,
 758:             research_context=research_context,
 759:             error_feedback=str(error_msg)[:2000],
 760:         )

 succeeded in 969ms:
 260:         diff_result = compute_agreement_score(different)
 261: 
 262:         assert sim_result["agreement_score"] > diff_result["agreement_score"], (
 263:             f"Similar ({sim_result['agreement_score']:.3f}) should score higher than "
 264:             f"different ({diff_result['agreement_score']:.3f})"
 265:         )

 832: def _build_restricted_env() -> dict[str, str]:
 833:     """Build a restricted environment for the subprocess.
 834: 
 835:     Passes only the variables needed for Python and data analysis libraries
 836:     to function. No API keys, no network configuration.
 837: 
 838:     Includes SANDBOX_READ_DIR and SANDBOX_WRITE_DIR for controlled file
 839:     access to evidence files and analysis output.
 840:     """
 841:     env = {}
 842: 
 843:     # Python needs these to find its stdlib and packages
 844:     for key in ("PATH", "PYTHONPATH", "PYTHONHOME", "SYSTEMROOT", "TEMP", "TMP",
 845:                 "VIRTUAL_ENV", "CONDA_PREFIX", "USERPROFILE", "HOME",
 846:                 "APPDATA", "LOCALAPPDATA"):
 847:         val = os.environ.get(key)
 848:         if val is not None:
 849:             env[key] = val
 850: 
 851:     # Matplotlib needs a writable config dir
 852:     env["MPLCONFIGDIR"] = tempfile.gettempdir()
 853: 
 854:     # Prevent matplotlib from trying to use a GUI backend
 855:     env["MPLBACKEND"] = "Agg"
 856: 
 857:     # NumPy/OpenBLAS thread control (prevent fork bombs)
 858:     env["OMP_NUM_THREADS"] = "1"
 859:     env["MKL_NUM_THREADS"] = "1"
 860:     env["OPENBLAS_NUM_THREADS"] = "1"
 861: 
 862:     # Sandbox file I/O directories for scripts that need evidence access
 863:     sandbox = _prepare_sandbox_env()
 864:     env["SANDBOX_READ_DIR"] = sandbox["SANDBOX_READ_DIR"]
 865:     env["SANDBOX_WRITE_DIR"] = sandbox["SANDBOX_WRITE_DIR"]
 866: 
 867:     return env

 869: 
 870: def _extract_json_from_output(raw_output: str) -> dict | None:
 871:     """Try to extract valid JSON from output that may contain non-JSON lines.
 872: 
 873:     Scripts sometimes print debug output before the JSON. This function
 874:     scans for the last JSON object or array in the output.
 875:     """
 876:     # Try to find the last { ... } block
 877:     lines = raw_output.strip().split("\n")
 878: 
 879:     # Strategy 1: Try parsing from the last line that starts with "{"
 880:     for i in range(len(lines) - 1, -1, -1):
 881:         stripped = lines[i].strip()
 882:         if stripped.startswith("{"):
 883:             candidate = "\n".join(lines[i:])
 884:             try:
 885:                 return json.loads(candidate)
 886:             except json.JSONDecodeError:
 887:                 continue
 888: 
 889:     # Strategy 2: Find the outermost { } pair
 890:     first_brace = raw_output.find("{")
 891:     last_brace = raw_output.rfind("}")
 892:     if first_brace >= 0 and last_brace > first_brace:
 893:         candidate = raw_output[first_brace:last_brace + 1]
 894:         try:
 895:             return json.loads(candidate)
 896:         except json.JSONDecodeError:
 897:             pass
 898: 
 899:     return None
 900:

 902: def _extract_charts(parsed_result: dict | list) -> list[dict]:

 906:     "image_base64" data. Validates that base64 data decodes to valid PNG.

 910:     charts = []

 913:         raw_charts = parsed_result.get("charts", [])
 914:     elif isinstance(parsed_result, list):
 915:         raw_charts = parsed_result
 916:     else:
 917:         return charts
 918: 
 919:     if not isinstance(raw_charts, list):
 920:         return charts

 787: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
 788: # Internal helpers
 789: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
 790: 
 791: def _run_subprocess(
 792:     cmd: list[str],
 793:     stdin_data: bytes | None,
 794:     timeout: int,
 795:     cwd: str,
 796: ) -> dict:
 797:     """Run a subprocess synchronously (called via asyncio.to_thread).
 798: 
 799:     Returns dict with returncode, stdout, stderr strings.
 800:     """
 801:     import subprocess
 802: 
 803:     try:
 804:         proc = subprocess.run(
 805:             cmd,
 806:             input=stdin_data,
 807:             capture_output=True,
 808:             timeout=timeout,
 809:             cwd=cwd,
 810:             # Restrict environment: only pass essential variables + sandbox paths
 811:             env=_build_restricted_env(),
 812:         )
 813:         return {
 814:             "returncode": proc.returncode,
 815:             "stdout": proc.stdout.decode("utf-8", errors="replace"),
 816:             "stderr": proc.stderr.decode("utf-8", errors="replace"),
 817:         }
 818:     except subprocess.TimeoutExpired:
 819:         return {
 820:             "returncode": -1,
 821:             "stdout": "",
 822:             "stderr": f"Process killed after {timeout}s timeout",
 823:         }
 824:     except Exception as exc:
 825:         return {
 826:             "returncode": -1,
 827:             "stdout": "",
 828:             "stderr": f"Process error: {str(exc)[:500]}",
 829:         }

  69: +def _validate_ast(script: str) -> tuple[bool, str]:
  70: +    """AST-based validation: import allowlist + reflection-attribute blocklist.
  71: +
  72: +    Closes the regex bypasses found in Codex iter-1..5 review:
  73: +    - comma-separated imports (`import json, socket`)
  74: +    - indirect __builtins__ reflection
  75: +    - frame-reflection (`sys._getframe().f_builtins`)

  80: +    - `__class__.__bases__[0].__subclasses__()` chain (mitigated by
  81: +      blocking `__subclasses__` attr but the `__class__` chain start is
  82: +      caught too)
